Excellent! The fix has been applied successfully.

## Summary

**The Fix:**
Changed the format specifier in line 1344 of `lustre/utils/liblustreapi_nodemap.c` from `%s` to `%u`.

**Rationale:**
The compile error occurred because the `fprintf` statement was using the wrong format specifier for the `offset` parameter. The `offset` parameter is declared as `__u32` (unsigned 32-bit integer), but the format string used `%s`, which expects a `char *` (string pointer). 

The correct format specifier for an unsigned 32-bit integer is `%u`. This matches how `offset` is used elsewhere in the same function (e.g., line 1359: `snprintf(param, sizeof(param), "%u+%u", offset, limit);`).

This was a simple type mismatch error introduced during the refactoring when the nodemap functionality was moved from `obd.c` to the library. The original code in `obd.c` likely had `optarg` (a string) in that position, but the library API changed it to accept a `__u32` directly.

Perfect! I've successfully fixed all the compile errors. Let me provide a summary of the changes:

## Summary of the Fix

**Problem:** The patch introduced compile errors due to unused variable declarations in `lustre/utils/liblustreapi_nodemap.c`. The compiler was treating warnings as errors (`-Werror=unused-variable`), causing the build to fail.

**Root Cause:** Five functions had declared a local variable `int rc = EXIT_SUCCESS;` that was never actually used. These functions were returning `errno` directly instead of using the `rc` variable.

**Fix Applied:** Removed the unused `rc` variable declarations from the following five functions:

1. **`llapi_nodemap_test_nid()`** (line 414) - Removed `int rc = EXIT_SUCCESS;`
2. **`llapi_nodemap_fileset_del()`** (line 695) - Removed `int rc = EXIT_SUCCESS;`
3. **`llapi_nodemap_add_offset()`** (line 986) - Removed `int rc = EXIT_SUCCESS;`
4. **`llapi_nodemap_del_offset()`** (line 1022) - Removed `int rc = EXIT_SUCCESS;`
5. **`llapi_nodemap_del_idmap()`** (line 1111) - Removed `int rc = EXIT_SUCCESS;`

**Rationale:** These functions all follow the same pattern - they set `errno` to the negated result of `nodemap_cmd()` and then return `errno`. The `rc` variable was declared but never assigned or used, making it completely unnecessary. Removing these unused variables eliminates the compiler warnings and allows the build to succeed.

Here's summary of my changes:
Excellent! The fix has been applied successfully. Now let me provide a summary of what was fixed:

## Summary

### The Compile Error Fix

**Error:** 
```
liblustreapi_nodemap.c:67:3: error: implicit declaration of function 'register_ioc_dev'; 
did you mean 'llapi_register_ioc_dev'? [-Werror=implicit-function-declaration]
```

**Root Cause:**
The patch added new nodemap API functions to `liblustreapi_nodemap.c` that needed to register the OBD device for ioctl operations. The code incorrectly used `register_ioc_dev()` instead of the correct function name `llapi_register_ioc_dev()`.

**Fix Applied:**
Changed line 67 in `lustre/utils/liblustreapi_nodemap.c` from:
```c
register_ioc_dev(OBD_DEV_ID, OBD_DEV_PATH);
```
to:
```c
llapi_register_ioc_dev(OBD_DEV_ID, OBD_DEV_PATH);
```

### Rationale

1. **Correct Function Name**: The function `llapi_register_ioc_dev()` is the proper API defined in `include/libcfs/util/ioctl.h` and implemented in `lib/libcfs/l_ioctl.c`. It's used throughout the codebase (e.g., in `obd.c`, `portals.c`, `svcgssd.c`, etc.) to register device IDs for ioctl operations.

2. **Consistent with Existing Code**: The patch moved nodemap functionality from `obd.c` to `liblustreapi_nodemap.c`. The original code in `obd.c` (line 3195) correctly used `llapi_register_ioc_dev()`, so the new code should use the same function.

3. **Prevents Implicit Declaration Error**: Using the correct function name ensures the compiler can find the proper declaration in the header files, eliminating the implicit declaration warning/error.

### Note on the Second Error

The second error about `-Wno-gnu` is a compiler flag configuration issue unrelated to the code changes. This is likely a build system configuration issue that would need to be addressed separately in the Makefile or build configuration, but it's not caused by the patch itself.

Here's summary of my changes:
## Explanation of the Fix

**Problem**: The `jt_nodemap_modify` function had an incorrect `fprintf` call with a format string mismatch.

**Root Cause**: After the refactoring in the patch, the error message was incorrectly trying to print the `cmd` variable (an `enum lcfg_command_type`, which is an unsigned int) using the `%s` format specifier. This caused two errors:
1. Type mismatch: `%s` expects `char*` but got `unsigned int`
2. Too many arguments: The format string had 5 `%s` placeholders but 6 arguments were provided

**Solution**: Removed the `cmd` argument from the `fprintf` call on line 4812. The error message now correctly prints:
- `%s` → `jt_cmdname(argv[0])` - the command name
- `%s` → `nodemap_name` - the nodemap name  
- `%s` → `param` - the parameter name
- `%s` → `value` - the parameter value
- `%s` → `strerror(errno)` - the error description

This matches the format string's 5 `%s` placeholders with 5 string arguments, and removes the erroneous `cmd` enum value that was being passed.

Patch Set 20:

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

This service is only provided in hopes to be useful and reduce latency from push to getting actual results in the face of trivial code errors

Here's summary of my changes:
## Explanation of the Fix

**Problem**: In the `jt_nodemap_modify()` function at line 4812, the error message was incorrectly formatted:

```c
fprintf(stderr,
    "error: %s: cannot modify nodemap '%s' to param '%s': value '%s': %s\n",
    jt_cmdname(argv[0]), nodemap_name, cmd, param, value,
    strerror(errno));
```

**Issues**:
1. The format string has 5 `%s` placeholders
2. Six arguments were provided: `jt_cmdname(argv[0])`, `nodemap_name`, `cmd`, `param`, `value`, `strerror(errno)`
3. The `cmd` variable is of type `enum lcfg_command_type` (an integer), but was being passed to a `%s` format specifier which expects a string

**Solution**: Removed `cmd` from the argument list. The corrected line now reads:

```c
fprintf(stderr,
    "error: %s: cannot modify nodemap '%s' to param '%s': value '%s': %s\n",
    jt_cmdname(argv[0]), nodemap_name, param, value,
    strerror(errno));
```

**Rationale**: The error message is meant to show which parameter modification failed. The `param` variable already contains the property name (e.g., "admin", "trusted", etc.), so including `cmd` (the internal enum value) was redundant and incorrect. The fix aligns the number of format specifiers with the number of arguments and ensures all arguments match their expected types.

Patch Set 28:

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

This service is only provided in hopes to be useful and reduce latency from push to getting actual results in the face of trivial code errors

Here's summary of my changes:
## Summary

**Fix Applied:**

I removed the unused static variables `mds_device` and `oss_device` from `lustre/tests/llapi_nodemap_test.c` (lines 24-25), keeping only `mgs_device` which is actually used in the code.

**Rationale:**

The compile error occurred because:

1. **Unused variables**: The static variables `mds_device` and `oss_device` were defined but never referenced anywhere in the code. The compiler flag `-Werror=unused-variable` treats this as an error.

2. **Why they were unused**: The patch moved the `nodemap_cmd` function from `obd.c` to `liblustreapi_nodemap.c`. In the original `obd.c`, there were helper functions `get_mds_device()` and `get_oss_device()` that used `cur_device` (a global variable in that file). The test file appears to have been created with these static variables in anticipation of using them, but the actual test functions call `llapi_get_mds_device()` and `llapi_get_oss_device()` directly instead of using the static variables.

3. **Why `mgs_device` is kept**: Unlike the other two, `mgs_device` is actually used on line 67 in the `test1()` function as a parameter to `llapi_name2dev()`.

The fix removes the dead code, allowing the compilation to succeed with the strict warning flags enabled.
